And then extract that to the forepart, and then you will see that which has been understood from those with a sharp instrument of the one part into which you know that all the meat is removed; for if there remains in him any cause for which the abscission is possible, then you rate that with one of the subtle instruments with facility into which he has not remained any cause. But if it is lorded over with blood or there is a boil, then you place to him that which you will; or if it is of the malignant boils, then cut and cauterize that into which bleeding is abscinded and all the caves are open.
And then it shall be removed from the nose, when the incision is made, with wine and water or vinegar. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds moisture into the palate, then you know that it is healed.
But if the moisture does not penetrate according to that which you do, then you know that inside him is meat in the pus sub-bones of the nose to which no abscission has been arrived.
Therefore then do so you interpose bile to him of which there is any grossness, and in him move mots, nuts, and pause between each nut the quantity of the finger or less, and enjoin the patient and interpose one end of the bile in the nose with the ray or another cause by which it is possible to him.
And after that which has been done, let him throw his breath into that which arrives at the canals of the nose, and be breathed over his gullet, for troops like this seem to do this action, and it is a slight cause to that which he wants to do.
And then pause the two ends of the bile, one end that goes over the nose and another which goes into the nose, and then administer a scissor of meat with the nuts that are in the bile, and do so until you know that the meat is removed from the nuts of the bile.
And then pull out the bile, and pause in the nose the abstraction of blood a sponge , and do so for three days or more until the gum has corroded all that which is separated from the meats.
And then at the end of the cause, pause in the nose a cannula of lead for several days until it is healed.
But if you find that the cure is exhausted, use that.
And this is the form of the instrument to head-purger with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nose:
And do so from silver or iron, which is like a little open lamp, likewise with a little hole, and the meat similarly.
And if you want, make a cannula closed likewise with cane, and the cannula of the instrument to head-purger and be flat, uncovered; to which is handle in his arse, with which you have that when you heat in him oil or water that you want of the sucks and the causes.
Chapter XXV.
Of the yls in the ends of the nose.
Many times it is born theyl in the ends of the nose, and is magnified and swollen for several days until what is stopped to him.
And because of that you insert that in the commencement of the appearance of him, and withdraw it altogether. And then pause over the place or cautery or medicine burning which is in the place of him.
But if the incision is delayed until it is magnified, then consider whether it is suppuration, hard, of dusky colour and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron because it is boil; for many times to that which you insert this suppuration becomes great malice on him who had.
And if the boil is of the colour not dusky and there is incision possible in all that, then evacuate the patient and insert that without fear, and bind it around until it is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of the suture of the nose and of the lips and of the ear when the connection is dissolved by water or like.
Know that when there happens solution of continuity in one of these cartilages, few confer in that operation unless in some men.
Therefore do so when also for some cause of those that you consider whether it is fresh water with his blood, and then join the two lips of the wound with suture, and then heal that until it is healed.
And if the lips of the wound have already been separated and each has healed, then you must scrape away any dead flesh from the wound so that it may bleed. Then, tie the two lips of the wound together tightly and put on powdered dragon's blood and crushed aspen wood over it, then apply a layer of diafinicon plaster or one of the other consolidative plasters, and leave it on for two or three days, then remove that plaster and replace it with another, and leave it on until the flesh has healed naturally.
But the manner of the suture is to bring the wound together or with needles as we have recommended in the suture of the belly, or bring the wound together with thread in such a way that you and your assistant know how it was done.
Chapter .XXVII.
Of the extraction of those causes that come from both lips within the wounds.
Many times in these wounds between the lips of men you will find certain hard bumps resembling grains of ergot, and some are small while others are large.
Therefore, you must turn the lips inside out and cut into each of those hard bumps from all sides, then fill the wound with powdered sage until the bleeding is stopped, then wash the wound with wine vinegar and treat it with something astringent until it is healed.
Chapter .XXVIII.
Of incision of the flesh pressed against the gums.
Often there is flesh pressed against the gums, which the ancients called albus, so you must lift that up with a hook or what you have there, and cut it at its root, and let the pus flow out or the blood.
Then place powdered sage or other astringent or drying powders on the wound.
And if that flesh comes back, cut it again secondly, and cauterize it, because then the cautery will not let it come back.
Chapter .XXIX.
Of reason of teeth with iron.
When there are rough, sharp sores on the surface of the teeth in the wounds and holes between the gums and also within the gums, some are black and are made yellow or green by corruption of the gum and the teeth are made loose.
Therefore, you must put the patient between your knees and hold his head in place, and pull the teeth in which those sores appear and the causes seem like sand so that no cause remains inside them, and this removes the blackness and yellowing and others until they are cleansed.
Therefore, if that is the end of what is in the beginning of the root, then that is good; but if not, then you must go back over the root on those teeth again and again on the second and third day until it reaches the final state that you want.
And know that teeth have many needs for various tools of different shapes according to how they are prepared for your operation. And therefore the file with which the tooth is filed for the wound between the teeth is another type of file than that used to file between the teeth according to other forms, and you should prepare those types of files which you will see immediately.
Chapter .XXX.
Of extraction of teeth.
You must cure the tooth of its pain by all means and delay at all costs in complete extraction of it, because there is no cause that exceeds the appearance of it when it has been extracted, for it is a subtle substance that is an obstacle in its extraction.
But when the patient is forced to have that tooth extracted, then you must be certain which is the painful tooth, for many times the pain deceives the patient and it appears to be in a healthy tooth, and you extract it and yet the pain does not cease until the painful tooth has been extracted, because we have seen this through the operation of the barbarians.
Therefore, when you are certain which is the painful tooth and that you know it, then you must scrape around the circuit of the tooth with a spatular in which there is some virtue so that it dissolves the tooth from the gum entirely all around, and then pull it out by its roots with your fingers or with fine forceps little by little until you loosen it.
And then grab it tightly with strong fingers or strong pliers, and hold the patient's head steady so that he does not move, and pull the tooth according to the right method so that you do not break it or give the patient greater pain.
And if there is a cavity, then take one of those instruments and put it below the tooth from all sides with ease and force the extraction of it just as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is cracked or hollow, then you must fill that crack with a piece of cloth and squeeze it with the end of a thin rod so that it is not broken when you tighten it on it with your fingers.
And you must open it widely with a scarification around the circuit of all parts of the gum and be very careful that you do not break it or tear it apart, and return to the patient because the first pain of it is great.
And be careful that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their haste and audacity in the extraction of them, for they do not follow what we have recommended; because many times they bring great illnesses on men which are very difficult to cure, and their roots are all worn away or some of them, or that you extract it with certain bones of the jaw just as we have tested.
And then the extraction of it should be washed with wine cauterium or vinegar with salt.
And if blood flows out of it, therefore, as we have said before, take some quantity of salt and sprinkle it on the wound, and if that salt does not stop the bleeding, cauterize it.
The shape of the forceps and thin tongs with which the tooth is extracted at the beginning should be long, narrow-tipped and thick, so that they do not bend when you operate with them.
And let them also be as wide of handle in the middle so that when you tighten them they do not bend, they should be short in length.
And let them be made of Indian iron forged and hammered, and in their tips be teeth with which the others bite into each other and tighten with a strong descent, and sometimes the tips of those are the shape of the beak of an owl, so it is hooked, and they are of strong constriction.
Chapter .XXXI.
Of extraction of teeth and the dislocation of the bones of the jaws that are broken.
When you must extract a tooth that is broken due to some cause, then you should hold the wound closed with a bandage for one or two days until the wound is softened; and then use the instrument or forceps whose tips are joined together like the beak of an owl or hooked, the shape of the forceps:
Their tips should be made with pliers or a file.
And if it does not obey you with those forceps or tongs, then you should cut into the root and strip away all the flesh and put in the instrument called the lever, which is a short lever whose shape is as follows:
Let there be a small one of short thickness, and not so wet that it is not broken.
Therefore if through this the vein is cut, it is good; and if not, use some other instrument of which these are the forms: The form of the first instrument is triangular in its extremity, and in which there should be some thickness.
The shape of the second instrument is that it should have a triangular and very fine point.
And now you are helped with this instrument having two spikes, and whose form is as follows: and with other instruments which are used in pulling teeth; for it is done with this instrument which is like the jaw of a large animal, and this is its form:
of the triangular bent point, short or curved, and in which there should be some thickness, and not wet enough to break.
And another wisdom is that the instruments of the teeth move and are like other instruments.
But the wise and subtle artist will find for himself many ways according to what he learns from the operation and various illnesses; for there are various illnesses which the ancients did not describe or use proper instruments for because of their different shapes.
But if the bone of the jaw or other bones in the mouth are broken, then the foot must be cured where it is convenient with some of those instruments and forceps which we mentioned in the extraction of teeth roots, and use the action for which this is the form:
And some thickness must be applied little by little, and the hole held closed with the mouth so that it does not open or escape until all the bone is healed; then restore the area with appropriate medicines for this.
But if it is a small fracture, then cut away the fracture and the blackness from it, and cure the area inside until it is healed.
Chapter XXXII.
Of the cure of teeth protruding above others.
When teeth protrude not according to their natural shape, and especially when they do so in women, and especially in older women, then you should consider: if the tooth is next to another tooth and there is no way of closing or binding it, then cut it; but if the tooth is next to another tooth, then drill it with this instrument whose form is like a pig's jaw, and which is made from Indian steel with a very fine point.
And your drilling should be such that you drill it for several days according to the hardness of the tooth, and that none of the other teeth are harmed.
And if the protruding tooth is worn away by grinding, then grind it with an Indian steel file whose form is as follows:
And all of it is made from Indian steel, and the point is very fine; and it is like small needles, and with the file which is used to make needles, the tooth is ground little by little over several days with ease, so that no other tooth is harmed or worn away. Then line it at the end, and cut it with a very sharp razor.
And if the tooth of which one side is broken and cuts the tongue, then you should grind it until that fracture is flattened and rounded off, so that the tongue is not cut nor the speech impaired.
Chapter XXXIII.
Of restoring broken teeth with gold or silver foil.
When teeth are knocked out and broken due to a blow or fall, and the patient cannot chew, and your cure with styptic medicines has not helped, then in order that they do not rot, they must be strengthened with gold foil rather than silver, for silver turns black and rots within a few days, but gold never changes.
And the foil should be so fine and thick according to how much can fit between the teeth; and the form of the repair is that you take the foil and place twice as much between two healthy teeth, and then it grows with two curves of the foil between two broken teeth, or if one or more are broken, until it reaches the healthy tooth on the other side. Then repeat the bonding inside at the break from which you started, and strengthen your work with ease and skill so that none of it is broken.
And your bonding should be such that you bond the foil so that it does not open at the roots of the teeth.
Then cut away the excess foil with tweezers or pliers, and add those to each location with action, and cover them over and conceal them between the healthy tooth and the broken tooth, so that they do not harm the tongue. Then let it be bound thus tightly with thread.
But if it is loose or torn, strengthen it or those with another foil in the same way at all times.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the repair of two healthy teeth and two broken teeth, as they are bound thus:
And when one or two teeth fall out and return to their places, and are regrow thus as we have described, and rot again:
Then let it not be done except by a wise artist.
And sometimes it is appropriate to use some cause of cow bones, and it is made in the form of a tooth, and placed in the hole from which the tooth fell out, and strengthened as we have said, and remain and serve with that for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
Of the cutting of the ligature which appears in the tongue, and prohibited speech.
This ligature which appears under the tongue sometimes naturally, or accidentally occurs due to a blow which has already healed.
And the operation is to open the mouth of the patient, and lift up his jaw bone which is under his tongue; and then insert that nervous ligament according to its breadth so that the tongue is released from its binding.
But if there is any hardness or knotting in it, and that is due to the hardening of a blow, then you cut and split it according to its breadth so that you have split the ligament and the knot is dissolved.
And be careful that there is not any fissure in the flesh of the jaw, and that you split only the membrane, and there is a flow of blood.
Then let it be washed with vinegar or with sour wine, and then place the tongue in its socket, so that there is a wound which the patient does not close so that it is not healed again.
But if blood flows, then place a piece of charred wood over the hole; but if the blood stops, then cauterize the hole with a cautery which is appropriate for this. Then let it be cured by the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXXV.
Of the extraction of a ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes there occurs under the tongue an abscess which resembles a small lump, and it prevents the tongue from its natural movement, and when it is enlarged and fills the mouth:
And the operation is to open the mouth of the patient and examine the abscess.
And if you see it of a dusky or black colour, hard, to which the patient does not respond with feeling, then do not touch it for it is rotten.
And if it is white, and moist, then place the tip of the needle in it, and split it with a very fine point; and if blood flows while you are operating, then pause over it with charred wood, so that the blood is stopped.
And then return to your task, washing the wound with wine and salt, and treat it with another ointment until it is healed.
Chapter 36.
Of the extraction of an abscess from both ears, and that which occurs in the throat, and of other abscesses.
When there is swelling in the throat, there are glands which are united like cotton, and which become enlarged and are called two ears; when you treat them with what we have said in the division, and they do not heal, then consider whether the abscess is hard, of dusky color, and of little feeling; then touch it not with iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is large, then touch it not with iron through the flow of blood; before you let that be matured, either you will pierce that or it will burst by itself.
And if it is of white color, soft and the root of it subtle, then that one is to be incised.
And the operation upon it is that you consider, before your operation, whether the abscess has rested with complete rest or if it has diminished by any diminution; and then let the patient lie before the sun, his head in your lap, and open his mouth, and the servant take hold of his tongue with his hands, away from the instrument most noble of which this is the form:
And it shall be made of silver or of bronze, and it shall be subtle like a needle.
Therefore when you press with that the tongue and it is shown to you the abscess, and put upon that your instrument, then take hold of it and insert that into the hole outward as far as you can. Another one is that you pull on some of the membranes; then incision that with an instrument of which this is the form:
Another one is that you pull on some of the membranes; then incision that with an instrument of which this is the form: and it is like tweezers, except that the ends of it are curved so that the openings of each one is in the direction of the other, very sharp, and it shall be made of iron tempered hard.
But if this instrument is not present to you, then incision that with spatulum of which this is the form: And it shall be sharp on one side, not sharp on the other side.
And after you have incised one part, incision the other according to this manner of incision, and then let the patient recuperate from water rubbed on.
But if there ensues a flow of blood, recuperate with water of decoction of husk of pomegranate or leaf of mallow, and similar to that from the causes constrictive until the flow of blood is restrained, and then cure that until it is healed.
And sometimes in the throat there are other abscesses other than those two ears; and incision them according to what you see and say in the incision of two parts alike.
And I was once treating a woman of an abscess which was occurring in her throat; and that abscess was of dusky color, of little feeling, which had closed her throat, and the woman was breathing with difficulty, and she had prohibited eating and drinking water, and she was brought to the point of death unless she had stood for one or two days.
And that abscess had grown so much that it had made two holes through which pus was flowing.
Therefore I cut the throat carefully and put in one of them a probe, and drew out that pus and a great part of it, and then I incision the other side from where I understood the other tract; and then I opened the mouth of him, and grasped his tongue, and then I put the probe into that abscess.
And then I cut out a great part of it, and there flowed from it only a little blood. Therefore the throat of that woman was completely opened, and she began at once to drink water, and then to take food; therefore I did not cease to incision that abscess many times for a long time, and an abscess succeeded in place of that one which I incision until it was prolonged.
Therefore I had the throat of her cauterized and then sewed it up, therefore from that I walked around and did not know what God made of that one.
Chapter 37.
Of incision of membrane when it is abscessed.
When catarrh occurs in the uvula, and it is abscessed and is long, then it is named perpendicular; and if it is at its lower part thick and round, then it is named buba.
But when it is healed with what you have said in the division and your treatment does not confer, and then there occurs that the abscess cauterized is last from her and is subtle; and if it is to that length and is bloody, of dusky color or black, and is not to him sensible, then beware that you incision it for in that one is fear over the patient.
And when you see that according to the manner that I have said of its whiteness and length, then make the patient lie down and press his tongue with an instrument of which you have described the form, and then put the probe in the new one, and draw that downward and incision it with one of two instruments of which you have said in the incision of two parts.
And beware that you incision it except what is adjusted over the natural term for addition, for if you incision from it more, you will break his speech.
And then the incision, use what we have recommended in the incision of two parts, and cure that one until it is healed.
But if the patient was frightened by the incision of him, beware that you use gentleness in the cauterization of him without fear, and the manner of the cautery in him is only with sharp water; and it shall be that you lay the head of the patient in your lap, and then press his tongue with the instrument which we have said, and then take of the water which we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and confer with that live cause, and pause that not thick nor subtle, and of that fill the concavity of the instrument of which this is the form:
Let the end of it be hollow in which is paused the medicine as with the concavity of spoon of ray; and pause the instrument with the medicine over the uvula, and the patient let lie on his side so that flow saliva or mucilage of the mouth of him because no any cause descend over the throat of him and that it thaws that.
And then hold your hand with the medicine, and express that over the uvula for the space of a half hour until you see that to be blackened and dulled by the biting of the medicine.
And if you wish, take thread and wrap that over the end of the ray; and immerse the thread in the medicine and insert the ray with the thread into a cannula of above so that the thread adheres in that cannula, and do that as many times until you accomplish what you wish of the cauterization of the grape, and then let it dry that for three or four days.
And if indigestions that repeat the medicine, repeat that, and then the cauterization cleanse in the circuit of the grape with thread immersed in wine, and cleanse with that what is in the circuit of it of the medicine; and be washed with rubbed water, and be cured with ointment, and teeth with remedies until it is healed.
And this kind of cure is more safe than incision and longer lasting in terms of fear.
Sometimes the uvula is cured by something more subtle than cauterization and incision; it is cured by sub-fumigation in this way: take calamus, hyssop, oregano, rue, Arabic thistles, camomile, bromides, and similar ingredients from among the herbs, and prepare all of those things, or some of them, in a bowl, and let them be submerged in agreeably sour wine, and let the wine boil; and let the bowl be properly luted, and let there be a hole in the middle of the bowl through which an appropriately-shaped instrument made of silver or copper is placed; it should be made of silver or copper.
And the end of this instrument is inserted into the patient's mouth so that the steam rises to the uvula over the glottis, as the uvula becomes very fogged up.
And you should repeat this several times until it is dry; be careful not to perform this cure during the beginning of an appetite for food, because it will increase the appetite too much; rather, you should wait until after he has eaten something.
But if you do not have this instrument available, then take a reed and attach some wool to its end, so that the patient's mouth is filled, because the wool prevents the steam from burning the mouth.
And this cure is good for health.
Chapter 38.
On the extraction of thorns and what adheres in the gullet, and other causes.
Many times there are adherences in the gullet or a thorn in the throat or some other cause.
Therefore, you should extract whatever is visible there, by pressing the tongue with an instrument in front of the sun, so that what is in the throat will be revealed to you.
And if what is hidden in the throat is not apparent to you, then make the patient vomit before the food has digested in the stomach; because often the cause of an obstruction in the gullet is thrown up by vomiting; or the patient should swallow a piece of soap or a piece of lettuce stem or a piece of dry bread; or he could take a piece of dried sea sponge, and chew it hard while spitting out the saliva, and then press his throat with your hand, because when this reaches the place where there are thorns, they will come out. Or take an eel and chew it with vinegar, and let it be inside the mouth and spit it out; or take a pig's ear and chew it and then spit it out.
But if they are not dislodged by the causes we have mentioned, then use a lead instrument in the following shape:
And the point should be made with a plucker, and the point should be larger than the rest of it; and in the end of it there should be a concavity which you insert into his throat with ease.
And let him hold his head up, and be careful not to touch the bone of his throat, so that it does not push against the bone or the thorn, or that the doctor with his hand.
But let the patient himself put it in, according to his knowledge of where the obstruction is located and let him press down from above, and pull up the instrument with his hand, according to the amount by which he is prepared for it to be dislodged.
Chapter 39.
On the extraction of blood clots from the gullet.
When blood clots are treated with what we have said in the division of cures by medicines and not by cauterization, then look to the gullet of the patient from above, as you press his tongue with an instrument which we recommended.
Therefore if you see the blood clot, extract it with a small needle or with very fine tweezers, gently and decently.
And if it is not possible for you to extract it with that, then take a hollow reed and insert it into the patient's gullet, and then place a red hot iron in the concavity of the reed, and do this as many times as necessary (as long as the blood clot is dead and comes out of his throat), and let the patient abstain from drinking water for the whole day.
And then take a rag wet with water, and wipe his mouth with it; and do not spit out any of the water and let him sip the water little by little with his hand, because the blood clot will come right away when he feels the water.
But if it is not dislodged by what we have recommended, then sub-fumigate the patient with camphor or asafoetida through the instrument which we recommended in the sub-fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, as long as it is necessary.
And there is another way of operating with sub-fumigation: take a bowl in which are burning coals and the bowl should be covered with a cloth in the middle of which there is a hole, and fix the end of the instrument in that hole; then do the sub-fumigation; and let the patient close his mouth over the end of the reed, so that the sub-fumigation does not escape as long as you know that the sub-fumigation has reached the blood clot, because the blood clot will come right away.
And if it does not come out, then repeat the sub-fumigation many times; and let the patient abstain from drinking, and eat salty causes and alms, and do not drink water; and if this treatment is followed, then the blood clot will be dislodged.
And this is the form of the instrument with which blood clots are extracted from the gullet when they are seen; and it is similar to tweezers except for the fact that there is some curvature in it. This should be inserted into the gullet, and its end is similar to a stork's beak, which is hooked, so that when it grasps something, it does not let go; therefore, when you press on some cause, it will not slip.
Chapter 40.
In which is the sum of the tongue in regard to obstructions and their sections.
Obstruction are of many kinds, according to what is remembered by us in this book.
And they are diverse in their penetration and sections by two methods: the first is by the nature of obstructions themselves; and by what we understand from moisture.
And the second method is by the places where they occur: for example, an obstruction that accidentally occurs in the head is different from one that accidentally occurs in the anus; and an obstruction that occurs in a fleshy part is different from one that occurs in a joint; and each of them is treated by operation.
And there are some obstructions which do not need to be penetrated, but only the maturation of the pus in them or the completion of them.
There are also obstructions which do not need to be punctured but only the maturation of the pus in them or their completion: or they are near a joint, for when an obstruction occurs near a joint, its nature is prolonged by the parts around it and it strongly corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint; or it is near the main member, so if you delay its penetration until it matures, then it will corrupt the main member; or it is near the anus, so do not puncture it until it matures. May you know the time of the piercing of the pustule, and that is when it has matured.
And you will know that it has matured when there is a lessening of the pain and fever, and also a decrease in redness and pulse, and a sharp point to the head of the pustule, and other signs.
And you will know that the piercing has been successful when it occurs in the lowest place of the pustule and pus comes out from the healing of the prominence.
And the piercing should always be done along the length of the skin or body, if the pustules are on the palms of the hands or soles of the feet, and in places of the veins, nerves, or arteries; and, finally, in any place where there is no reflection; for in those places where there is a reflection, use piercing according to that member.
But when the pustule is on fleshy tissue, it is better to let the piercing be done within it as it has been stated; for if you pierce that which precedes it, the body of it is prolonged and the pus flows out from it along with a lot of thick matter, and its lips are hardened and the depth of it.
But some pustules should be pierced according to the width of the skin or body, depending on the necessity, or according to that member from which one suffers.
And you must administer a small piercing on the smaller pustules, and for the larger pustules, a large and ample piercing or many piercings according to the variety of their sizes.
And there are others that are pustules in which the cord is hollow and has been cut, when it is done so that a pan is made from it, that is, as much as one can make from a horse's hoof, or from a bullock's hoof, or even more.
And there are those that are cut with a three-pronged incision, and there is one in which it is cut like the shape of a fern leaf, just as the pustules on the angles of the nose.
And there are those in which a round incision and a moon-shaped one is administered, and they are similar to those.
But if it does not happen like that with superficial pustules, then you must pierce that one with a superficial piercing, or a flat one only.
And when the pustule is large and has already collected a lot of pus, pierce that one and do not be afraid to extract all of its pus at that time; first draw out some from it, then plug up the pustule until the next day, then draw out a larger portion, then do this many times according to its degree until it is fully drained.
And especially if the patient is of cold nature, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an old person in weakness, for the animal spirit is many times resolved by the discharge of pus, and soon dies after, then you operate on them.
Therefore, keep this chapter with great caution, and when you pierce those pustules, wash the sores, and then consider if the sore of the pustule is little, or is a flat section, then you administer the remedies of lead or of red copper; and if the pustule is large, and its fissures are many, then you must pause the needle in each crack as they come out together.
And if in the pustule a part of the cord is abscised or you have hollowed it out all around, then you must complete it with old lead, or with thread made from linen or from lead cloth, just as when one treats pans or roots, without moisture; and strengthen that one on the third day; and then process and cure it with what one uses to heal sores.
But if blood flows in the hour of your operation, then you must administer water mixed with vinegar and wine in which a cloth of lead has been soaked, and place that over the location of the flow of blood many times.
But if the flow of blood persists, then you must administer remedies and cures and powders which I have mentioned in many places in this book and its divisions.
But if it is in the winter time, and the location of the pustule is the site of many nerves, then you must mix powder with wine and oil that is hot, and place those on the locations.
And if it is in the summer, and the locations are fleshy, then you must place powders that have been moistened with water and oil or wine and oil on them; and let all of this be done until the third day, just as we have said, and then you must dissolve the pustule and wash it and administer to its cure whatever is convenient for it.
And that is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of pustules universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said about every pustule in which manner is the way of its cure specifically.

Of the incision of the pimple of the swelling within the throat.

Chapter 45.
Of the sections of the types of nodules.
There are many types of nodules, and I have already described all of their types in the division.
And one should thus account for the difference between a nodule and an ulcer as long as there is doubt.
Therefore I say that with an ulcer there is heat, fever and violent pains until the ebullition of the superfluity ceases; it is completed putrefaction, and then the fever, pain and heat cease as well.
But with a nodule, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains that which the lion has in its throat, a proper sac.
And they are according to the color of the body, and their origin is with a hernia, and they are made in such a way that it can be major or minor; and they are of two types: either fatty and containing moisture, and the colors of moisture are many, according to what I described in the division.
Therefore, when one arrives at the cure of nodules, he should probe and investigate it to its origin with an instrument that is called an introme, according to its form in the chapter that is next.
And it is the method of investigation of ulcers and all nodules; take this instrument and insert it into the most moist part of the ulcer, and rotate your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the membrane.
Then close your hand according to the size of the ulcer and extract the instrument and consider what has come out in its wake.
And if moist matter of any color comes out, then open it up with a superficial incision as I have said for the other ulcers.
And if you do not get moisture from the instrument's passage, then know that it is fatty.
And dry it out with an incision in the shape of a cross according to this form: In the same way that it is taught, and suspend it with pins, and scrape away the membrane from every part with ease, and guard the skin or sac, if you can, on it, and extract that pus with the nodule.
But if it is broken in the operation and it is not possible to extract that pus all at once, then take it in bits so that no cause remains within him.
Because if any cause remains within him, a little or a lot, the nodule will return according to the most.
And if you see that some little part remains within him, then complete the wound with some powdered caustic and strengthen the wound, and place over it what creates an ulcer cautery, and cure it by another remedy until it is healed.
And if it is a large nodule, then cut its two lips and cure it with that which incarnates.
But if the vein is pulsatile or not, then cut and pour into that place a mixture of three parts vetiver oil and one part lye, and let it rest for two days or three until the mixture hardens; then return to opening what is broken in the nodule.

Chapter 49.
Of the section of abscesses that occur through an artery or vein.
When an artery is broken and the vein is collapsed on it, then many times abscess occurs: for when the abscess is through an artery, it is longly aggregated in the bowels of the body; and when it is forced into the abscess with the fingers, you feel a quack in it that there is stridor.
And what is through a vein is round to the surface of the body.
And the section on this abscess is difficult, and especially in that which is below the armpits, and in the angle, and in the neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is large, therefore its cure by cautery is avoided, and that which is at the extremities, or to the head, must be avoided.
But for that which is from them by inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut it in the vein with a long section; and then open the section with nails, and the artery, and free the tunics so that they are discovered.
And then place over it an awl and make it penetrate to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which causes you to press on it in extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then puncture the place which is between two membranes with a needle so that blood flows out from it all that is in it, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then apply cure to which is engendered pus within so that the membranes fall, and then cure it with appropriate ointments until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess from the section of a vein, then you must hold with your hand what is possible to you of the abscess with the vein, and then insert the awl below the place which you have held with your hand, and make it penetrate; and there will be in it double thread within so that you draw out that from the other side, and then tie the abscess with a fine thread according to what we have said to you in the thread of two parts with two extremities.
But if you fear that the thread is drawn out, then insert the awl so that it penetrates all the abscess because of the first puncture of the awl, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in its middle part so that when it is soaked what is in it, then you cut the superfluity of the vein, and leave what from it is tied.
And then pause over it powder which you have soaked in wine and oil, and then apply the cure which is made with water and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 50 of the abscess which occurs by twisting of nerves.

And it is not a pustule located in the chest area, but rather below the neck, and he is sick all over, and he does not want to go forward or backward.
Therefore, for those who have pain in their joints, it is not advisable to use a hot iron, because it would quickly cause contraction.

And if it is large, then open it with a knife, and remove the pus; and close the wound with stitches, and heal it so that it may recover.
Chapter 11:
Of the incision of a pustule which happens to the jaw and happens in the stomach.
Some people have many warts on their stomachs and other parts of their bodies, which are called warts because they resemble fungi, the roots of which are fine but the tops are thick; sometimes their lips are also affected, and they can be either small or become very large.
And I have seen one such person whose two warts in his stomach were very similar to fungi; their roots were fine and they were not different in color.
And sometimes the lips of these people turn inside out and split open, and moisture runs from them all the time.
Therefore, when I cut into one of these, I found that it was about an inch and a half deep. The other was about an inch deep.
And when you cut into them, consider whether the patient is hot or cold, and if the color of the tissue is white, then cut it with a wide knife, and let it be cauterized in the fire, for many times the pus is expelled through the incision; and if blood comes out, cauterize it.
And if you see the patient is fearful and anxious, do not cut it with a hot iron; but rather take some fresh pitch, and spread it on that area, in the manner we have described; and let it rest for two days.
Then tighten the pitch around the thread; therefore, do not stop tightening the large thread around it until it is completely cut off and falls away by itself.
But if the wart has a thick root, then cutting it will cause fear and terror, especially when it is in the stomach.
But you may cut only half of it, and then cauterize it so that it does not return.
Then heal the wound so that the wound recovers.
And beware of cutting a wart which is dark in color, has little sensation, and seems to be very firm, for that one is cancerous.
And I have seen many such warts, just like cranes.
Chapter 12:
On the treatment of an umbilical hernia.
Umbdominal hernias are caused by many things; or by fissures in the diaphragm above the stomach, and the tissue or intestine of which they are made goes into other openings; or by blood coming from a vein or artery in front, or by restricted expansion in it.
But if it is from a fissure in the diaphragm and from an injury to the tissue, then the pustule will be of similar color to the rest of the body; it will have less pain, and it will appear at various locations. And if it is from a hernia of the intestine, then its location will be as we have described before, with greater and more violent diversity; and when you press on it with your fingers, it hides away, and soon returns; and it becomes very large because of internal heat and violent effort.
But if it is from moisture, then there will be pain, and it will not hide when you press on it with your fingers, nor be constricted or cut off.
And if it is from blood, then the pustule will appear with dark-inclining marks.
But if it is from fat, then it will be a heavy, large and hard pustule, and it will be according to a certain amount.
And if it is from expansion, then touching it will cause pain.
And the operation on it is that you should consider whether the umbilical hernia is from blood of an artery or vein, or from expansion; then you must not use the cure for it as we have instructed in the chapter where we spoke about hernias from arteries and veins.
And if the umbilical hernia is from the intestine or tissue, then you must tell the patient to hold his breath and be standing upright; then touch around the whole circumference of the umbilicus, and then command him to push his stomach out towards your hands over his chest, and then cut the hernia open at its highest point with a wide knife all the way around where you have touched it with the tip; then extend the opening to the sides above it with a large needle; and then tie it all the way around with strong pitch or strong thread in a decent manner.
Then open the hernia wide over the wound and put your finger into that hole and feel for the intestine; and if you have it caught or trapped by the ligature, then cut off the hernial sac and push out the intestine to the sides inside the abdomen.
And if you have caught the tissue, then take it with a needle; and cut away its excesses.
But if it is against an artery or vein, then surround it a lot and then return to your operation; and take two needles and put them in strong pitch and insert two needles around the hernia in the shape of crosses, making them penetrate; then tighten the hernia into four parts over the needles.
And if you want to, take away the needles and leave that place where the extended flesh is shrinking in and falling by itself; or cut it when it has become fine and is shrinking in, and then heal it with what covers it inside so that it may recover.
And if the umbilical hernia is from fat in it or moisture, then you must hollow out the pustule as we have said and draw away the blood or moisture which you find in it; then heal it with what covers it inside so that it may be consolidated.
Chapter 13:
On the treatment of a hernia.
We have already said, in the division, about the kind of hernia and how it is treated with remedies, and that it is difficult to treat a hernia with an iron without causing an ulcer; we have also spoken about a hernia generated from the mother and the caution in treating it.
And the ancients said that sometimes a hernia can be in a place where its removal is possible, like a hernia which is in the breasts or in the thighs and which resembles the limbs attached to drawing out all of it, especially when it starts small.
But when it is old and large, you must not come near it, for I have not seen any such hernia recover from that.
And the operation on it is when it has been located as we have said, that you must precede and cut away the patient and purge them from black bile, then bind that hernia, if there is a manifest herniation discovered.
Then prepare the patient with a preparation in which he will be operated on, and cut off all the nails of his toes; and then with a good sharp knife cut deeply into the tissue all around so that no cause remains from the roots. And let the blood flow freely without stopping it; and then squeeze out all of it from the wound by pressing with your hand or an instrument that you can manage, according to which instrument is available to you.
But if you are facing difficulties with the blood flowing from a vein or an artery, then cauterize that area so that the flow of blood is stopped; and then treat it with another treatment so that it heals.
Chapter .liv.
Of the treatment for dropsy.
We have already described, in the division, of the species of dropsy and the signs of each species; of the treatment for it with medicines.
And the one which is cured with iron is only the species of "althitas", and it is not approach iron for the species of tympany or of iposarca because they are deadly.
And when you have treated this species of dropsy timpanistre with medicines and it does not respond to your treatment, then consider; because if the patient is already weakened, or has another malady like another dropsy, as if it is in the chest or abdomen and similar to those, then beware that you do not treat it with iron, because there is danger in this.
But if you see the patient has robust vigour and does not have another malady except dropsy, and he is neither an infant nor elderly, then the manner of operating on him is that you raise the patient between your hands and press his abdomen with your hand, forcing the water out from under the navel; and then take a hollow thorn according to this form:
It should be of two pointed parts long, of acute extremity like a thorn; but it should have in it some shortness little by little, so that during the operation you do not pass into the intestine and that you take it out.
And then consider if the generation of dropsy is from part of the intestines; because in that case you should lengthen yourself from the navel by the quantity of three fingers at the lower ends, on the right side of him over the navel.
But if the generation of dropsy is from a malady of the liver, then your section should be on the left of the navel by three fingers.
And if it is from a tumour, then your section should be on the right side.
And you must not make your section over the side that the patient wants to lie on so that the superfluities do not flow to that place freely.
And then pierce all around with the instrument and insert into that section, and raise your hand with the thorn between the skin and the bowels, and squeeze it out; and if a nail or a little bit.
And then pierce the bowels so that the thorn reaches the desired place which is where the water is. And then take it out and insert an instrument of which this is the form: And it is like a slender silver tube; made of silver or of brass or of lion’s tooth, to which at the lower end there are two small holes, and on the sides of it three holes: two from one side and one from the other side; and its end is notched according to the manner of a pen, like this:
And at the upper end of it there is a ring, because when the instrument reaches the water, then it immediately rises over the instrument, therefore it empties from the water in the momentary quantity; because if you empty more than that which does not happen in the moment, he will soon die by resolution of his animal spirit, or it happens to him five times that is near death.
But it empties according to the quantity of his vigour and according to how you understand the dispositions of the patient from the vigour of his pulse and from its goodness.

And sometimes it is caused by swelling, and sometimes there is a crack in the intestine, and here it is retained, and it causes great pain of the patient, and sometimes it causes worse pain when it is pressed.
And in the cure of the species of this illness with iron there is danger, for it must be avoided in that.
The manner of the operation for this is to command the patient to reduce the intestine with his hand to the parts within its cavity if he obeys your instructions, and then he should be bent forward at the waist between your hands, and you should raise up his legs.
Then tie the cord which binds the testicles to the parts above, and cut through the whole length of the cords of the testicles; and place hooks on both lips of the incision according to your instructions for opening the incision with them.
And if it is possible, make the incision according to how much you can manage to have the hernia pushed out through it.
Then cut away all of the tissues which are beneath the cords of the testicles, as long as you can see the hard white membrane covering each part.
Then you should insert your finger into the space that is underneath the testicle, between the white membrane and the membrane of the hernia, and cut away any adhesions you find there at the back of the hernia.
Then pull the cords of the testicles towards you from outside, and while doing so stretch out the white membrane on top with your left hand, and lift up the hernia by the membrane to the edge of the incision; and command an assistant to hold the hernia in place as you dissolve any adhesions behind it using a suitable solution.
And check with your fingers that there is no cause for the intestine being wrapped up in the hard white membrane. But if you find any cause for it in him, then you should send him back to bed.
And pierce through the part below the cords of the testicles by an incision through which blood and pus can flow out as we have recommended before.
And apply a pad soaked in oil and place it over the wound; and apply the stitches we have recommended (and sometimes the white membrane is cauterized as we have said at the incision where there is fear of a flow of blood, for in some cases this happens), and leave the stitches so that they can fall out on their own.
But if it is delayed, then it should be soaked in water and placed over the wound so that it falls out as we have said.
And then heal the wound with the other method of healing wounds when it has healed.
Chapter 66.
Of a hydrocele.
In this hernia I have not seen anyone who has been cured by the application of iron.
And the first thing is that it is done as we have recommended in the hernia which occurs with wine; that is, you should ligate the vessels at the incision there with ease, and then dry up the pus in the region around it as it drains out.
And heal the wound as we have said until it is healed.
Chapter 67.
Of the rupture which occurs in the groin.
Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin as we have said, and the region protrudes.
And there should be no cause for the intestines to enter the groin; and if they do, that is rare; and return them inside at every hour.
But if the time is prolonged, there is an opening in the membrane through which the intestine descends into the membrane; and this happens because of the extension of the membrane at the groin as we have said, which causes it to be stretched out and become soft and swollen, and an abscess forms and protrudes.
And its cure is by cauterization as we have recommended before the description of it.
And sometimes it is cured by iron according to this method: and the patient lies on his stomach between your hands, and then you dry up the rupture of the abscesses which protrude with an incision according to its length within the space of three fingers.
And then tighten up the white membrane which is underneath the cords so that it is uncovered.
And then take a bandage and place it over the protruding part of the membrane, and press it against the abdomen.
And then sew together the two prominent parts at the end of the bandage around the membrane, and adjust them with stitches on both sides.
And then tie off the end of the bandage, and do not cut into the membrane at all, nor extend the hernia, nor any other cause as we have said in the cure for intestinal hernia.
And then heal that with the cure of wounds, and when you have inserted the threads, cleanse it and restore the wound until it is consolidated; because the membrane is contracted and the protrusion of the rupture is reduced.
And cauterization is better in this place, because pus is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
Of the softening of the cords of the testicles.
Sometimes the cords of the testicles in some men are softened because the flesh which is between them is softened, and they lack the necessary strength.
Therefore it is necessary in the cure of him who lies on his stomach according to his condition, and that all the softened cords which are on top of the natural cords be tightened up, and then sew together both lips.
And if you wish, cut off in the beginning the surplus of the softened cords with three or four incisions and with a firm stitch.
And then insert between the stitches; and then heal by the cure of the other wounds until it is healed and the threads have fallen out.
Chapter 69.
Of castration.
You know that castration in our law is forbidden, but it was remembered to me that I should mention it in this book; and it is not necessary for me to remember it except in two ways, one of which is for the sake of the physician when he is questioned about it, so that he knows how to cure it if it happens; and the other way is that we sometimes need castration of other beasts for our young ones, as with horses, oxen, pigs, and similar animals.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by strangulation or by incision at an opening.
But when it is done by strangulation, the way to do the operation is that we make the beast lie on its side in water so that his genitals are softened and are long and that they hang down. Then take your hand away so that they are resolved and do not appear beneath the touch.
But in a castration done by incision and cutting, you must hold the animal and squeeze the cord of its testicles with your left hand.
Then lift up the scrotum, and cut into each side with an incision so that two processes can be inserted.
Then cut those so that you have excised them. And do not let any cause be upon the body except for the subtle head which is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better which is done by compression because compression strongly leaves no cause in the testicles that the animal desires coitus.
Then cure the wound until it is healed.
Chapter .lxx.
Of the cure of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men is according to two types: the first is when there appears a growth in the cord of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles, the shape of a clitoris in which there are female-like genitals.
And sometimes urine comes from that which is in the cord of the testicles.
But in women there is one kind: and it is that the vulva of the woman on the clitoris is like two testicles of a man, a little bit smaller at the entrance as well as the foreskin of a man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three kinds: two from men and one kind from women. And it is so that you cut into those tight meats until the pressure of that escapes, and then cure those with the cure of other wounds.
And for the second kind of men from which urine comes that is in the cord of the testicles, there is no cure nor operation on him.
Chapter .xxi.
Of léntine and prominent meat from causes in women.
Lentige is strongly tightened over natural causes in that it is and becomes tight, and sometimes it is magnified in some women so much that it becomes like men's and goes into coitus.
Therefore you must have the superfluity of léntine with your hand or a needle, and cut into it.
And do not cut all the way through, especially in the part of the vein, so that it does not cause a flow of blood.
Then cure that with the cure for wounds until it is healed.
But prominent meat is meat that grows in the womb of the mother and fills it up; it usually comes out at the openings according to the appearance of a tail (and for this reason some first called it "tailed malady"); therefore we cut into it as we cut into léntine, and cure it until it is healed.
Chapter .lxxii.
Of the cure for elephantiasis.
Elephantiasis is when the vulva of a woman is not perforated or has a small hole. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental it is due to a malady which has preceded it, and it is caused by tight meat or subtle swelling or thickness.
And it is caused either in the womb of the mother or in her ribs or in the upper part of her body or in the lower part, and it prohibits coitus and conception and childbirth, and it usually prohibits menstruation as well.
And the diagnosis of it is made by examination of the midwife, if the swelling is apparent, then it is near the vagina; but if it is not apparent, then you seek that out with your fingers or with a rod.
But if the swelling is due to subtle swelling and it is near both labia, then you cut into it and burst it open.
And it is so that you pause over both labia and also pause your fingers indicating the space in between with both hands.
And let the woman be on her back, her legs extended, and then extend both labia with force so that the subtle swelling is broken open and the perforation is opened.
And then take wool and dip it in oil and place it over the wound, and let it be for a day so that the wound is not closed.
But if the swelling is large and thick, then you cut into it with a spatule or with a blade of myrrh.
But if the perforation is due to meat, then suspend that with a needle and cut into it.
And you have the medicines that make the flow of blood stop without biting, like ahacatia and dragon's blood and onions, bound with egg white from an egg.
And then administer a wide lead bandage so that the wound is not loosely closed.
And hold it for some days and administer cold water.
Then it will be cured by the other cure of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes accidents happen in the mother's womb with other meats, and then you cut into them according to this way. But if it is due to an abscess in the head, then do not do anything to that abscess in any way.
Chapter .lxxiii.
Of the cure for hemorrhoids and of a tail and of red botul which happen in the vulva of women.
Hemorrhoids are the appearance of orifices of many veins from which flows a continuous flow of blood; and when they are old hemorrhoids and they are like thumbs.
And I have already said in the division of those and their signs, and tell them also which ones receive cure and which do not.
Therefore I say that hemorrhoids and thumbs when they are in the womb of the mother and do not appear in the feeling, then in those there should be no cure with a needle.
But those which are in the orifices of the mother over which there is feeling, then those that are cured.
And let the woman be in warm water and then extend it with the fingers or with rough cloth, or cut into it with sharp instruments.
And then sprinkle over those the flow of blood from one of the sprinkling powders without biting, like ahacatia and similar to those.
And then let her feet be parched for an hour, and then place it in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then do that which is cooked in a mixture of hemp and pomegranate and walnut shells and similar things.
And take flour of barley and cook that with honey and sour wine and make a plaster with that over its back.
And if the blood is scanty, then boil it; and if not, attach two ventouse, and to the nipples its incision.
And take wool and dip it in juice of yarrow or in juice of marshmallow or in juice of wild celery with cooked wine, and make a plaster with that over the wound; and then cure the wound with unguents until it is healed.
And cure that until it is healed.
Chapter .lxxiv.
Of accidental piercing of the head in the womb.
Here is the translation: And I have already described these diseases, their kinds and symptoms, as well as their treatments in the previous section.
Now I will describe in this treatise the kind of swelling that appears in the body when it is caused by humors, and if you want to know how to perform the operation on it using iron.
Now consider whether the pain of the swelling at its onset is acute with percussion and phlegm and fever, and see if it subsides when you press on it, then do not incise it, but treat it with something that helps to mature the humor until the acuteness of the accident passes.
Now you should make the woman lie down on her side with her hips raised and her back bent, and her feet placed at the lower part of the belly, and let her thighs be spread out, and place her arms below her ears, and hold them there with bandages in a comfortable position.
Then the midwife should stand on the right side and administer the instrument with which the opening of the womb is dilated, the form of which will depend on the causes that will be discussed next.
Now when you want to administer this instrument, you should lubricate the tip of the womb of the woman, and what goes into the womb from the instrument should not be larger than the size of the womb, and guide the patient. But if the instrument is larger than the size of the womb, then you should place powder on the texture of the opening of the womb so that the insertion of any instrument into the opening of the womb is prohibited.
Now you should pour the liquid that runs through the instrument from above, and let the minister hold the instrument and rotate the liquid while the opening of the womb is dilated.
And when the membrane appears and is touched by hand and is soft and moist, then you should dry its head with a sponge on the tip of the instrument.
